тАШрдпреЛ рдорд░реНрддреНрдпреЗрд╖реБ’ рдЗрддрд┐ рд╡рд┐рдВрд╢рддреНрдпреГрдЪрдВ рджреНрд╡рд┐рддреАрдпрдВ рд╕реВрдХреНрддрдВ рд╡рд╛рдорджреЗрд╡рд╕реНрдпрд╛рд░реНрд╖рдВ рддреНрд░реИрд╖реНрдЯреБрднрдорд╛рдЧреНрдиреЗрдпрдореН ред тАЬрдпреЛ рдорд░реНрддреНрдпреЗрд╖реБ ’ рдЗрддреНрдпрдиреБрдХреНрд░рдордгрд┐рдХрд╛ ред рдЕрд╕реНрдп рд╕реВрдХреНрддрд╕реНрдп рдкреНрд░рд╛рддрд░рдиреБрд╡рд╛рдХрд╛рд╢реНрд╡рд┐рдирд╢рд╕реНрддреНрд░рдпреЛрдГ рдкреВрд░реНрд╡рд╕реВрдХреНрдд рдПрд╡ рд╡рд┐рдирд┐рдпреЛрдЧ рдЙрдХреНрддрдГ рее

+Jamison Brereton

2 (298)
Agni
V─Бmadeva Gautama
20 verses: triс╣гс╣нubh
This hymn shares a number of features, including phraseology, with the previous one: like IV.1 it begins with the installation of Agni as the mediator of the sacri ficial exchange between men and gods, and it contains a brief, Indra-less account of the Vala myth (vss. 15тАУ17), with the Aс╣Еgirases explicitly compared to the poets of today besieging the treasure-holding pen of the sacrifice. However, the first few verses of the hymn (vss. 2тАУ4) enlarge on AgniтАЩs role as messenger announced in verse 1. The hymn also contains an elaborate treatment (vss. 6тАУ10, 13тАУ14) of the various ritual services rendered to Agni by the sacrificers, and Agni is urged to dis tinguish between those who do such service and other mortals (esp. vss. 11тАУ12). The final two verses (19тАУ20) summarize the fire-worship that has just been performed by the sacrificers, both actions (тАЬwe have performed,тАЭ vs. 19) and words (тАЬwe have spoken,тАЭ vs. 20), a common hymn-ending device. Preceding them is a mysterious verse (18), whose position suggests that it closes the Vala myth, but whose content seems at least superficially unconnected.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

Agni

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬHe who has beenplaced immortal among the mortals, the observer of truth, a deity triumphant among gods, the invoker of the gods, the most diligent sacrificer, Agni; he has been plural ced (upon the altar) to lighten (the ceremony) by his (lustre), and for the elevation of the worshipper, through oblations (in heaven).тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Amont the mortal: or, among mortal organs of sense, Agni being that of speech: agnir-v─Бg bh┼лtv─Б mukham pr─Бvi┼Ыat

+Jamison Brereton

He who has been installed as the immortal among the mortals, the god among the gods, the truthful one, the spoked wheel (of the sacrifice), Hotar, best sacrificerтАФto blaze with his greatness, to be roused by the oblations of Manu: Agni.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

There seem to be deliberate echoes in this vs. of the 1st vs. of the preceding hymn (IV.1.1) – esp. p─Бda b dev├│ dev├йс╣гu arat├нr nidh─Б╠Бyi corresponding to IV.1.1b dev─Б╠Бso dev├бm arat├нс╣Г nyerir├й; also IV.2.1a тАж m├бrtyeс╣гv amс╣Ы╠Бtaс╕е and IV.1.1f ├бmartyam тАж m├бrtyeс╣гv ─Б╠Б. The first p─Бda is identical to I.77.1c, which continues (I.77.1d) with h├│t─Б y├бjiс╣гс╣нhaс╕е тАж as in our p─Бda c.

On trisyllabic mahn─Б╠Б(restored as *mahin─Б╠Бby Holland & van Nooten Rig Veda edition, though as *mahan─Б╠Бby Grassmann; see also Oldenberg Noten), see comm. ad I.123.4.

With Oldenberg (Noten, not SBE; also Renou; Keydana, Infinitive im с╣Ъgveda, 54), I take ─лray├бdhyai as a causative inf. in passive construction, тАЬto be roused,тАЭ rather than GeldnerтАЩs intransitive тАЬum тАж zu fahrenтАЭ or Witzel Got┼НтАЩs transitive reflexive тАЬum sich тАж in Bewegung zu setzen.тАЭ Note 7b ├бtithim ud─лrat тАЬwill raise (you) up (as) guest.тАЭ

+Griffith

THE, Faithful One, Immortal among mortals, a God among the Gods, appointed envoy,
Priest, best at worship, must shine forth in glory . Agni shall be raised high with man’s oblations.

+Oldenberg

He who has been established as the steward among the mortals, the immortal, righteous one, and among the gods, being a god himself, the Hotri, the best sacrificer shall mightily flame 1; Agni shall rise up 1 with the offerings of Manus.

+Geldner

Agni, der Unsterbliche unter den Sterblichen, der Gesetzestreue, der Gott unter den G├╢ttern als Rosselenker eingesetzt ist, um als bestopfernder Hotri m├дchtig zu brennen, um mit den Opferspenden des Menschen zu den G├╢ttern fahren.

+Grassmann

Der heilige, bei Sterblichen unsterblich, bei G├╢ttern Gott, ist eingesetzt als Opfrer, Als bester Priester, dass mit Glanz er strahle, erwachse durch des Menschen Opfer Agni.

+Elizarenkova

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬAgni, son of strength, genitive rated today at this our rite, as intermediate between both (gods and men) you proceed, the invoker (of the gods), harnessing, graceful Agni, your robust, vigorous, and resplendent steeds.тАЭ

+Jamison Brereton

O son of strength, o Agni, created here for us today, between both created (peoples [=men and gods])
you shuttle as messenger, o high one, having yoked your (horses) with their testicles stretched out (behind from speed), (the horses) bullish and blazing.

+Griffith

Born for us here this day, O Son of Vigour, between both races of born beings, Agni,
Thou farest as an envoy, having harnessed, Sublime One! thy strong-muscled radiant stallions.

+Oldenberg

Here, O Agni, son of strength, thou goest for us to-day as a messenger, thou who art born, between the two races (of men and gods), having harnessed, O tall one, thy puissant, manly, brilliant (stallions) 1.

+Geldner

Agni, du Sohn der Kraft, verkehrst heute hier geboren zwischen beiderlei Geborenen als unser Bote, nachdem du Recke die bullenartigen und hellfarbigen Hengste mit straffen Hoden angeschirrt hast.

+Grassmann

O Sohn der Kraft, uns heute hier geboren, o Agni, eilst du zwischen Gott und Menschen, als hehrer Bote, der du angeschirrt hast die lichten Stiere, deren Glieder straff sind.

+Elizarenkova

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬI celebrate the ruddy, food-bestowing, water- shedding, and swifter-than-thought-going, steeds of him who is the truth; harnessing the brilliant pair (to your chariot), you pass between the deities of whom you are, and human worshippers.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

You pass between the deities: antar─лyase yuс╣гm─Бс╣Г┼Ыca dev─Бn vi┼Ыa ─Б ca mart─Бn, you go between, you the gods, and men; you is specified from Agni being a divinity; he goes to men to receive oblation, and to the gods, of whom he is one, to bear it to them

+Jamison Brereton

The two chestnut steeds of truth, strong(-backed), ghee-backed,
I consider to be swiftest (even in comparison) with mind.
Yoking these two ruddy ones, you shuttle between (all of) you gods and the clans here, the mortals.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

The two rhyme words vс╣Ыdhasn┼л╠Бand ghс╣Ыt├бsn┼л clearly form a rhetorical pair, though they have different origins and grammatical analyses, as their different accents show. ghс╣Ыt├бsnu- is generally taken as a bahuvr─лhi with the reduced form of s─Б╠Бnu- тАШbackтАЩ as 2nd member. See Oldenberg ad loc. and ad I.16.2, and cf., with a different designation of the same body part, ghс╣Ыt├б-pс╣Ыс╣гс╣нha-. However, this cmpd. has a complex relationship with the differently accented ghс╣Ыtasn├║- as well as ghс╣Ыta-sn─Б╠Б- тАШbathed in gheeтАЩ. See Scarlatta (661-62). As for vс╣Ыdhasn├║-, Grassmann takes it as a root-noun cmpd, with sn├║- for sn─Б, and glosses тАШSegen triefendтАЩ; Scarlatta (662) more or less follows this analysis, though he proposes several different morphological pathways. Debrunner (AiG II.2.930), a bit confusingly, takes it as a тАЬNachbildungтАЭ to ghс╣Ыt├бsnu- though containing a suffix - asnu- (sim. Oldenberg SBE). (Debrunner does not gloss it; Oldenberg тАШmightyтАЩ.) Witzel Got┼Н seem to take it as containing the same тАШbackтАЩ as ghс╣Ыt├б-snu-, tr. тАШvon hochgewachsenem R├╝ckenтАЩ. I agree with the general sense that vс╣Ыdhasn├║- has to have been influenced by ghс╣Ыt├бsnu-, hence my parenthetic тАШstrong(-backed)тАЩ, but it cannot have been formed in direct parallel because of the accent. I think it should be evaluated in the context of another nearby form belonging to тИЪvс╣Ыdh, viz. the irregular (pseudo-)participle vс╣Ыdhas─Бn├б- in IV.3.6, a stem that occurs 3x in the RV. Since that stem was part of our poetтАЩs repertoire, I think it possible that he could create a reduced form of the тАЬsuffixтАЭ - s─Бn├б- (intermediately *-sn├б-, just as -snu- is reduced from s─Б╠Бnu-) with further adjustment of the final vowel to match ghс╣Ыt├бsnu-.

The instr. m├бnas─Б must go with j├бviс╣гс╣нh─Б given the close relationship between the root тИЪj┼л and m├бnas- (cmpds m├бno-javas-, etc.) throughout the RV; the question is only how to construe the instr. with the splv. I take it as an instr. of quality, rather like RenouтАЩs тАЬles plus rapides par rapport ├а la pens├йe (m├кme).тАЭ Flg. S─Бyaс╣Зa., Geldner tr. the phrase as if it were a comparative with an abl.: тАЬтАж schneller als den Gedanken,тАЭ which certainly makes sense but airbrushes the grammar. Witzel Got┼Н seem to take m├бnas─Б as a dual acc. (тАЬdie beiden schnellesten Denkorgane des с╣ЪtaтАЭ), which is grammatically impossible for neut. m├бnas- (expect *m├бnas─л). Masc. du. -as-stems do have the ending -─Б, but if the word here is meant to be masc., it should either be in a cmpd. (type su-m├бnas-) or show accent shift to a derived poss. adj. *man├бs- тАШhaving mindтАЩ, which is not attested. Others (L├╝ders 454, Scarlatta 662) simply detach m├бnas─Б from j├бviс╣гс╣нh─Б and tr. it elsewhere in the clause, but the formulaics speak strongly against that.

In the second hemistich the 2nd sg. verb ─лyase and the 2nd pl. acc. prn. yuс╣гm─Б╠Бn comes awkwardly into English (тАЬyou [sg.] speed between you [pl.] and тАжтАЭ), but neatly signals AgniтАЩs natal affiliation with one of the two sides for which he acts as go-between. See also 1a m├бrtyeс╣гv amс╣Ы╠Бtaс╕е, 10b dev├│ m├бrtyasya, where AgniтАЩs divinity is juxtaposed with his mortal worshiper(s).

Contra Oldenberg (SBE and Noten) and Geldner, I see no reason to take m├бrt─Бn (or, as Oldenberg wants to read, *m├бrt─Бm) here as gen. pl. It is perfectly interpretable as an acc. pl.

appositive to v├н┼Ыaс╕е. However, the same form in 11b is a somewhat harder case; see comm. there, as well as nс╣Ы╠Д╠Бn in vs. 15.

+Griffith

I laud the ruddy steeds who pour down blessing, dropping oil, flectest through the thoualit of Order.
Yoking red horses to and fro thou goest between you Deities and mortal races.

+Oldenberg

Harnessing the two mighty, red steeds that swim in gheeтАФ(the steeds) of Rita, I think, that are most swift with their mind 1, the ruddy ones, thou goest (as a messenger) between you, the gods, and the tribes of men 2.

+Geldner

Deine beiden hochgewachsenen, r├╢tlichen, schmalzr├╝ckigen Renner des rechten Werks halte ich f├╝r schneller als den Gedanken. Du schirrst die beiden Rotf├╝chse an und verkehrst zwischen euch G├╢ttern und den St├дmmen der Sterblichen.

+Grassmann

Ich seh’ im Geist des Heil’gen Flammenrosse, die schnellsten, die von Fett und Segen triefen; Die Flammen schirrend gehst du zwischen beiden, den G├╢ttern euch und uns den Menschenst├дmmen,

+Elizarenkova

рд╣реЗ рдЕрдЧреНрдиреЗ рд╕реНрд╡рд╢реНрд╡рдГ рд╢реЛрднрдирд╛рд╢реНрд╡реЛрдкреЗрддрдГ рд╕реБрд░рдердГ рд╢реЛрднрдирд░рдердГ рд╕реБрд░рд╛рдзрд╛рдГ рд╢реЛрднрдирдзрдиреЛрдкреЗрддрдГ рддреНрд╡рдореН рдПрд╖рд╛рдВ рдорд░реНрддреНрдпрд╛рдирд╛рдВ рдордзреНрдпреЗ рд╕реБрд╣рд╡рд┐рд╖реЗ рд╢реЛрднрдирд╣рд╡рд┐рд╖реНрдХрд╛рдп рдЬрдирд╛рдп рдпрдЬрдорд╛рдирд╛рдп рдЕрд░реНрдпрдордгрдВ рд╡рд░реБрдгрдВ рдорд┐рддреНрд░рдВ рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░рд╛рд╡рд┐рд╖реНрдгреВ рдорд░реБрддрдГ рдЕрд╢реНрд╡рд┐рдирд╛ рдЕрд╢реНрд╡рд┐рдиреМ рдЪ рдпрд╖реНрдЯрд╡реНрдпрд╛рдиреН рджреЗрд╡рд╛рдиреН рдЖ рд╡рд╣ рдЗрджреБ рдЖрд╣реНрд╡рдпреИрд╡ ред рдЙрдГ рдкреВрд░рдгрдГ рее рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░рд╛рд╡рд┐рд╖реНрдгреВ ред тАШ рдЛрдЬреНрд░реЗрдиреНрджреНрд░ ’ рдЗрддреНрдпрд╛рджрд┐рдирд╛ рдирд┐рдкрд╛рддрдирд╛рджрд┐рдиреНрджреНрд░рд╢рдмреНрдж рдЖрджреНрдпреБрджрд╛рддреНрддрдГ ред рджреЗрд╡рддрд╛рджреНрд╡рдиреНрджреНрд╡реЗ рдЪ ’ рдЗрддреНрдпреБрднрдпрдкрджрдкреНрд░рдХреГрддрд┐рд╕реНрд╡рд░рддреНрд╡рдореН ред рд╕реБрд╣рд╡рд┐рд╖реЗ ред’ рдирдЮреНрд╕реБрднреНрдпрд╛рдореН’ рдЗрддреНрдпреБрддреНрддрд░рдкрджрд╛рдиреНрддреЛрджрд╛рддреНрддрддреНрд╡рдореН рее

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬPossessed, Agni, of good steeds, an excellent car, and abundant wealth, do you amidst these (worshippers) bring to the man who offers worthy oblations, Aryaman, Varuс╣Зa, Mitra, Viс╣гс╣Зu, the Maruts, or the A┼Ыvins.тАЭ

+Jamison Brereton

Among those (gods), convey Aryaman, Varuс╣Зa, Mitra, Indra and Viс╣гс╣Зu, the Maruts, and the A┼Ыvins
just here, to the person providing good oblations, o AgniтАФyou who have good horses, good chariot, good rewards.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

Unaccented gen. pl. eс╣г─Бm must refer back to yuс╣гm─Б╠Бn тАж dev─Б╠Бn тАЬyou godsтАЭ in 3d; evidently the poet only wants a selection of them to be brought to the sacrifice.

+Griffith

Aryaman, Mitra, Varuna, and Indra with Visnu, of the Gods, Maruts and Asvins-
These, Agni, with good car and steeds, bring hither, most bountiful, to folk with fair oblations.

+Oldenberg

O Agni, with thy good horses, and thy good chariot, rich in bounties, bring hither from among them (the gods) 1 Aryaman, Varuna, and Mitra, Indra and Vishnu, the Maruts and the Asvins, to him who offers good oblations.

+Geldner

Fahr von ihnen den Aryaman, Varuna, Mitra, Indra und Vishnu, die Marut und die Asvin her mit sch├╢nem Wagen, mit sch├╢nen Gaben zu dem Mann, der sch├╢ne Opfer bringt, o Agni!

+Grassmann

Den Arjaman, den Varuna und Mitra, den Indra, Vischnu, Murut’s und die Ritter, Die fahre her zum opferreichen Manne mit guten Rossen, Wagen, Sch├дtzen, Agni.

+Elizarenkova

рд╣реЗ рдЕрд╕реБрд░ рдмрд▓рд╡рдиреН рд╣реЗ рдЕрдЧреНрдиреЗ рдПрд╖рдГ рдорджреАрдпреЛрд╜рдпрдВ рдпрдЬреНрдЮрдГ рдЧреЛрдорд╛рдиреН рдЧреЛрднрд┐рд╕реНрддрджреНрд╡рд╛рдиреН рдЕрд╡рд┐рдорд╛рдиреН ред рдЕрд╡рдпреЛ рдореЗрд╖рд╛ рдЕрд╕реНрдп рд╕рдиреНрддрд┐ рдЗрддрд┐ рддрджреНрд╡рд╛рдиреН рдЕрд╢реНрд╡реА рдЕрд╢реНрд╡реЛрдкреЗрддрд╢реНрдЪрд╛рд╕реНрддреБред рдиреГрд╡рддреНрд╕рдЦрд╛ ред рдирд░рдГ рдХрд░реНрдордгрд╛рдВ рдиреЗрддрд╛рд░реЛрд╜рдзреНрд╡рд░реНрд╡рд╛рдиреНрджрдпрдГ рддрджреНрд╡рдиреНрддрдГ рд╕рдЦрд╛рдпреЛрд╜рдиреБрд╖реНрдард╛рддрд╛рд░реЛ рдпрдЬрдорд╛рдирд╛ рдпрд╕реНрдп рд╕ рддрдереЛрдХреНрддрдГ ред рд╕рджрдорд┐рддреН рд╕рджреИрд╡ рдЕрдкреНрд░рдореГрд╖реНрдпрдГ рдЕрдкреНрд░рдзреГрд╖реНрдпрд╢реНрдЪрд╛рд╕реНрддреБ ред рддрдерд╛ рдЗрд│рд╛рд╡рд╛рдиреНред рдЗрд│рд╛ рд╣рд╡рд┐рд░реНрд▓рдХреНрд╖рдгрдордиреНрдирдореН ред рддрджреНрд╡рд╛рдиреН ред рдкреНрд░рдЬрд╛рд╡рд╛рдиреН рдкреБрддреНрд░рдкреМрддреНрд░рд╛рджрд┐рдпреБрдХреНрддрд╢реНрдЪрд╛рд╕реНрддреБ ред рджреАрд░реНрдШрдГ рдЕрд╡рд┐рдЪреНрдЫрд┐рдиреНрдирд╛рдиреБрд╖реНрдард╛рдиреЛрдкреЗрддрдГ рд░рдпрд┐рдГ рдзрдирд╡рд╛рдиреН ред рд▓реБрдкреНрддрдорддреНрд╡рд░реНрдереАрдпрдГ ред рдкреГрдереБрдмреБрдзреНрдирдГ ред рдкреГрдереВрдирд┐ рдмрд╣реБрд▓рд╛рдирд┐ рдмреБрдзреНрдирд╛рдирд┐ рдзрдирд╛рджреАрдирд┐ рдХрд╛рд░рдгрд╛рдирд┐ рдпрд╕реНрдп рд╕ рддрдереЛрдХреНрддрдГ ред рд╕рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рдиреН рдЙрдкрджреНрд░рд╖реНрдЯреГрд░реВрдкрд╕рднрд╛рдпреБрдХреНрддрд╢реНрдЪрд╛рд╕реНрддреБ рее рдиреГрд╡рддреНрд╕рдЦрд╛ ред рдирд░реЛ рдпреЗрд╖рд╛рдВ рд╕рдиреНрддреАрддрд┐ рдиреГрд╡рддреН ред рдорддреБрдкреН ред рддрд╕реНрдп рдЫрд╛рдиреНрджрд╕рдВ рд╡рддреНрд╡рдореН ред тАШрд╣реНрд░рд╕реНрд╡рдиреБрдбреНрднреНрдпрд╛рдВ рдорддреБрдкреН’ рдЗрддрд┐ рдорддреБрдк рдЙрджрд╛рддреНрддрддреНрд╡рдореН ред рдмрд╣реБрд╡реНрд░реАрд╣реМ рдкреВрд░реНрд╡рдкрджрд╕реНрд╡рд░рдГ рее рее резрем рее

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬMay the sacrifice, Agni, be productive of cows, of sheep, of horses, and celebrated by your worshipper, aided by the priests, be ever uninterrupted; may it, mighty Agni, be productive of food and progeny, long continued, affluent, wide based, and held in full assembly.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

I.e. sabh─Бv─Бn, in the presence of spectators upadraс╣гс╣нi sabh─Бr┼лpayuktaс╕е

+Jamison Brereton

O Agni, a sacrifice bringing cows, sheep, horses, and manly comrades is never to be spurned.
Bringing refreshment and progeny, o Lord, it is long wealth, broad of base, fit for the assembly.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

The qualifier тАШlongтАЩ (d─лrgh├бс╕е) of wealth in d means, of course, тАШlong-lastingтАЩ (just as d─лrgh├бс╣Г t├бmaс╕е [I.32.10, etc.] refers to тАЬlong(-lasting) darknessтАЭ). However, since it is implicitly contrasted here with тАШbroadтАЩ (pс╣Ыthu-budhn├б- тАШhaving a broad baseтАЩ), it is clear that the image is one of physical dimensions, not merely temporal ones. And, at least for me, тАЬlong darknessтАЭ is a more striking verbal formulation than тАЬlong-lasting darkness.тАЭ

+Griffith

Agni, be this our sacrifice eternal, with brave friends, rich in kine and sheep and horses,
Rich, Asura! in sacred food and children, in full assembly, wealth broad-based and during.

+Oldenberg

This sacrifice, O Agni, is rich in cows 1, in sheep and horses, in manly friends; it is never to be despised; it is rich in nourishment, O wonderful lord 2, rich in offspring; it is long-lasting wealth, broad-based, with (brilliant) assemblies.

+Geldner

Das Opfer bringt Rinder, Schafe, Rosse, hat mannhafte Freunde, ewig denkw├╝rdig ist es, reich an Himmelsspeise und kinderreich, o Asura, ein bleibender Schatz, der auf breiter Grundlage ruht und gute Gesellschaft hat.

+Grassmann

Das Opfer, Agni, ausgef├╝hrt von Starken, ist reiches Gut an Rossen, Rindern, Schafen, an Speis’, o Gott, an Kindern und Gemeinden, weitreichend, festgegr├╝ndet, unvertilgbar.

+Elizarenkova

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬYou are the munificent recompenser of that man who, sweating (with toil), brings you fuel, and for your service causes his head to ache; protect him, Agni from every one that seeks to do him evil.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Munificent recompenser: svatav─Бn p─Бyuс╕е = dhanav─Бn p─Бlayit─Б, wealthy preserver

+Jamison Brereton

Whoever will bear fuel to you though sweating, or will scorch his head in serving you,
for him you will become a self-powerful protector, Agni. Make for him wide protection from everyone who bears malice.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

Having described in the previous vs. what a (properly performed) sacrifice can get us, the poet now tells us what we have to do to perform this sacrifice properly.

On the pf. subjunctives here, see my 2016 тАЬThe Vedic Perfect Subjunctive and the Value of Modal Forms to Tense/Aspect StemsтАЭ (Fs. J L. Garc├нa Ram├│n], with disc. of the pf. subjunctives in this verse as well as the pres. and aor.

subjunctives in vss. 7-9. There I specifically dispute K├╝mmelтАЩs interpr. (340, also 212, 595) of the pf. subj. as functioning тАЬzur Bezeichnung der vollendeten Handlung f├╝r den generellen FallтАЭ (i.e., тАЬтАж gebracht hat,тАЭ etc.).

+Griffith

The man who, sweating, brings for thee the fuel, and makes his head to ache, thy faithful servant,-
Agni, to him be a self-strong Protector guard him from all who seek to do him mischief.

+Oldenberg

1 Be a self-strong protector, O Agni, of the man who in the sweat of his brow brings fuel to thee 2, or heats his head desirous to worship thee. Deliver him from every harmful man.

+Geldner

Wenn einer im Schwei├Яe Brennholz f├╝r dich tr├дgt oder sich deinetwegen den Kopf hei├Я werden l├д├Яt, so sollst du ihm ein selbstsicherer Sch├╝tzer sein, o Agni. Bewahre ihn vor jedem ├Ьbelwollenden!

+Grassmann

Wer, Agni, dir im Schweiss das Brennholz anlegt, und dir zu Liebe sich den Kopf erhitzet, Dem sei du, Agni, kr├дftiger Beh├╝ter, den sch├╝tze du vor jedem schlechtgesinnten.

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬMay a son, firm in (devotion) and liberal (in offerings), be born to him who presents (sacrificial) food to you when needing food, who gives you constantly the exhilarating (Soma juice), who welcomes you as a guest, and devoutly kindles you in his mansion.тАЭ

+Jamison Brereton

Whoever will bring food to you just as you seek food, will whet (you) down, will raise (you) up as the gladdening guest,
will, seeking the gods, kindle (you) here in his dwellingтАФin him let
wealth, rich in gifts, be steadfast.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

As he often does, Geldner takes cid as a simile marker, but I do not think that is a possible function of cid, and certainly in this case there is no need to interpret ├бnniyate as a simile: Agni is regularly depicted as a greedy eater.

Contra Grassmann, all standard modern tr. and comm. take ni┼Ы├нс╣гat (so Pp.; ni┼Ы├нс╣гan is also phonologically possible, though morphologically unlikely) as belonging to тИЪ┼Ы─Б тАШsharpenтАЩ (common with n├н), not тИЪ┼Ы─Бs тАШinstructтАЩ (not found with n├н). There are formulaic parallels with clear forms of n├н тИЪ┼Ы─Б; see GeldnerтАЩs n. 7b and esp. VII.3.5c. With Oldenberg it seems best to emend to *ni┼Ы├н┼Ыat. He takes it as a short-vowel subj. to the redupl.

pres. ┼Ы├н┼Ы─Бti. So also Hoffmann (Aufs. II, 445-46 n. 14). This is certainly possible, but it could also be a masc. nom. sg. act. part. to this same redupl. pres. Both a finite 3rd sg. in a rel. cl. and a part. would be accented on the stem (not the preverb) as here, and either form is contextually possible. It can simply belong3 to the string of subjunctives in this passage that express ritual service. But note p─Бda a of the previous vs. (6a), which has a subj. and a part. (jabh├бrat siс╣гvid─Бn├бс╕е); one could argue that in this sequence of vss. there is no more than one finite verb per p─Бda, though that is not a particular telling argument.

+Griffith

Who brings thee food, though thou hast food in plenty, welcomes his cheerful guest and speeds him onward,
Who kindles thee devoutly in his dwelling,to him be wealth secure and freely giving.

+Oldenberg

The man who brings food to thee who art desirous of food, he who stirs up 1 the cheerful guest and rouses him, the godly man who kindles thee in his dwelling: to him may belong lasting and generous wealth.

+Geldner

Wer dir wie einem Hungrigen Speise bringen wird, deine E├Яlust reizt, den erfreulichen Gast aufmuntert und gottergeben im Hause anz├╝ndet, bei dem soll der freigebige Reichtum eine bleibende St├дtte haben.

+Grassmann

Wer dir, wenn du begehrst, die Speise darbringt, den Freudentrunk dir reicht, den Gast verherrlicht, Wer fromm gesinnt im Hause dich entz├╝ndet, bei dem sei dauernd gabenreiche Habe.

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬPreserve from sin the liberal sacrificer who glorifies you morning and evening, and presenting oblations, does what is acceptable to you in his own abode, like a horse with golden caparisons.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

A┼Ыvo na sve dame hemy─Бv─Бn = suvarс╣Зanirmita kakс╣гy─Бv─Бn, having a girth made of gold, the epithet is applied to the horse, though separated by sve dame, in his own house

+Jamison Brereton

Whoever at evening, whoever at dawn will celebrate you, or offering an oblation will make you a dear (friend)
in his own houseтАФlike a horse with much spurring you will carry that pious man out of narrow straits.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

Because the loc. phrase sv├й d├бma ─Б╠БтАЬin his own houseтАЭ in c does not seem to fit the equine simile there, in the published translation I took it implicitly with ab. However, cf. I.143.4 agn├нс╣Г t├бс╣Г g─лrbh├нr hinuhi sv├б ─Б╠Бd├бme тАЬurge Agni on with songs here in his own home,тАЭ with a form of тИЪhi and the same loc. phrase. If the hapax hemy─Б╠Б-vant- is derived from тИЪhi (so Oldenberg, SBE and Noten, generally now accepted) and means something like тАШpossessing/receiving impulsion, much impelledтАЩ, the spurring or impulsion may refer to hymns and be happening in AgniтАЩs own home. So an alternative tr. might be тАЬreceiving the spurring (of hymns) in your own house, like a horse you will carry тАжтАЭ The separation of hemy─Б╠Бv─Бn from the simile ├б┼Ыvo n├б invites but does not require reading hemy─Б╠Бv─Бn primarily with the frame, not the simile.

+Griffith

Whoso sings praise to thee at eve or morning, and, with oblation, doth the thing thou lovest,-
In his own home, even as a goId-girt courser, rescue him from distress, the bounteous giver.

+Oldenberg

The sacrificer who praises thee in the evening and in the morning and gratifies thee; that liberal man thou shouldst bring across all distress, like a well-impelled horse 1, (dwelling) in his house.

+Geldner

Wer dich des Nachts, wer am Morgen lobt oder dich mit Opfergaben zum Freunde macht, dem Spender sollst du im eigenen Haus aus der Not helfen wie ein angesporntes Ro├Я.

+Grassmann

Wer dich besingt am Abend, wer am Morgen, wer opferreich willkommnes dir erweiset, Gleich wohlgepflegtem Ross im eignen Hause, den f├╝hr hinaus aus Drangsal, den Verehrer.

+Elizarenkova

English translation:

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬMay that prayer be agreeable to you, Agni, who are a gracious deity, (which is uttered) by the man with whose well-conducted sacrifice you are well plural ased young (of the gods), of whose (rites) when worshipping you may we be the promoters.тАЭ

+Jamison Brereton

Whose ceremony you will enjoy, AgniтАФa god enjoying the
well-positioned ceremony of a mortal, while you giveтАФ
just his ritual offering will be pleasing, o youngest oneтАФ(the man) whose strengtheners we will be when he does (you) honor.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

r├бr─Бс╣Зaс╕е in b is clearly the middle part. to тИЪr─Б тАШgiveтАЩ. This form appears frequently in this metrical position with just that meaning (e.g., in the preceding hymn IV.1.5c). However, given the 2nd sg. subj. j├║joс╣гaс╕е тАШyou will enjoyтАЩ at the end of the preceding p─Бda, I think it likely that there is a secondary association with the near synonym тИЪran тАШenjoy, take pleasureтАЩ and that r├бr─Бс╣Зaс╕е could be loosely interpr. also as a 2nd sg. pf. subj. with irregularly strengthened root syllable and wrong accent (contrasting with the properly formed pf. subj. r─Бr├бс╣Зas, -at, etc.).

Geldner unaccountably interprets h├│tr─Б in c as the Goddess of the Offering found in the ─Аpr─л hymns rather than as a common noun meaning тАШofferingтАЩ, an interpr. that severs c from the rest of the verse.

P─Бda d is a clear relative clause (y├бsya), though both Geldner and Renou render it as an independent clause. Their tactic is understandable because p─Бda c, the only main cl.

in the vs., has no overt antecedent for the rel. prn. in d. We must supply a тАШhisтАЩ with h├│tr─Б to produce the connection between c and d.

The identity of тАЬwe strengthenersтАЭ is a bit puzzling. The stem vс╣Ыdh├бgenerally refers to a god or gods who strengthen their worshipers. In X.147.3 it is used of s┼лr├н-s, human тАШpatronsтАЩ, but patrons should not be the 1st ps. speakers in Rigvedic discourse – rather it should be those who receive their patronage, i.e., the poets. I assume here it must refer to the group of ritual officiants, including the poet himself, and the person they are strengthening is the Yajam─Бna (or what will become the Yajam─Бna in later Vedic ritual).

+Griffith

Whose well-wrought worship thou acceptest, Agni, thou God a mortal’s gift, thou liberal Giver,-
Dear be his sacrifice to thee, Most Youthful! and may we strengthen him when he adores thee.

+Oldenberg

That mortal whose well-ordered sacrifice thou, as the god, acceptest, O Agni, as a liberal giver, may his worship 1 be welcome, O youngest god, (the Hotri’s work performed) for a worshipper whose helpers we may be.

+Geldner

Wenn du, der Gott, an eines Sterblichen wohlgetanem Opferdienst Gefallen hast, deine Gunst schenkend, o Agni, so soll diese Hotra befriedigt sein, o J├╝ngster. M├╢chten wir eines solchen Verehrers F├╢rderer sein.

+Grassmann

Welch’ Opfer du, o Agni, huldreich annimmst, als Gott des Menschen reiches Mahl empfangend, Das Opfer sei willkommen dir, o j├╝ngster, des frommen Mannes, dem wir gerne dienen.

+Elizarenkova

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬMay the wise Agni discriminate between virtue and vice between (virtuous and wicked) men, as a (groom distinguishes between) the strong and weak backs (of horses); enrich us with wealth accompanied by virtuous offspring; be bountiful to the liberal giver; shun him who gives not.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Cittim acittim cinavadvi vidv─Бn, may the sage (Agni) distinguish that which is to be known, cittim j├▒─Бtavyam puс╣Зyam or virtue, and acittim acetan─лyam not to be thought of, or p─Бpam sin; cittim and acittim are explained by j├▒─Бnam and aj├▒─Бnam, knowledge and ignorance; mart─Бn, mortals or men, has no epithets and are supplied: the comparison runs: pс╣Ыс╣гс╣нheva vit─Б vс╣Ыjin─Б ca, like backs bright, (k─Бnt─Бni) and ill-bearing (durvah─Бс╣Зi); for the horses and the groom, (a┼Ыvap─Бla)

+Jamison Brereton

Insight and lack of insight will the knowing one [=Agni] distinguish, like backs, straight and crooked, (like) mortals.
And for the sake of wealth and good descendants for us, o god, both grant Diti [/Giving] and make wide space for Aditi [/Boundlessness].

+Jamison Brereton Notes

Note the phonetic figure in a, with the repetition of ci, followed by vi, which is then doubled by vi(dv─Б╠Бn): c├нttim ├бcittiс╣Г cinavad v├н vidv─Б╠Бn.

On v─лt├б- see comm. ad IX.97.17.

It is tempting here to take m├бrt─Бn here as a short genitive plural (see 3d above), as Geldner and Renou do. However, in X.89.3 v├н y├бс╕е pс╣Ыс╣гс╣нh├йva j├бnim─Бni ary├б, ├нndra┼Ы cik─Б╠Бya тАж тАЬwho has distinguished the races of the stranger, like the (straight and crooked) backs (of horses),тАЭ the clear acc. pl. j├бnim─Бni тАШraces, peoplesтАЩ suggests that semantically similar m├бrt─Бn here can be the obj. of v├н тИЪci.

I see no reason to supply a verb in c (like Geldner); it can be easily construed with d.

The pair d├нtim тАж ├бditim in d recalls the c├нttim ├бcittim that opens the vs. The standard interpr. take d├нtim ├бditim as a positive/negated pair, understandably. But this requires one of the words to be positively valued and one negatively valued (not necessarily corresponding to the privative form). The problem is that each of the verbs that govern these accusatives (тИЪr─Б тАШgiveтАЩ, uruс╣гy├б- тАШmake wide space, deliverтАЩ) ordinarily takes positively valued objects. Attempts to give uruс╣гy├б- a negative sense (e.g., Oldenberg SBE тАЬkeep off AditiтАЭ) founder on the large number of positive cases. I therefore think that d├нtim ├бditim are not in an etymological relationship but are actually a pun. d├нti- is the тАШgivingтАЩ goddess and derived from тИЪd─Б тАШgiveтАЩ. For this etymological relationship see VII.15.12 d├нti┼Ы ca d─Бti v─Б╠Бryam тАЬAnd Diti gives a thing of value.тАЭ ├бditi- by contrast is both the familiar goddess Aditi and the common noun тАШboundlessnessтАЩ (derived from тИЪd─Б тАШbindтАЩ). Each of these is the object of an appropriate verb: a different root meaning тАШgiveтАЩ for d├нti- тАШgivingтАЩ, a verb meaning тАШmake spaceтАЩ for ├бditi- тАШboundlessnessтАЩ. For a different wordplay with ├бditi- see previous hymn, IV.1.20.

+Griffith

May he who knows distinguish sense and folly of men, like straight and crooked backs of horses.
Lead us, O God, to wealth and noble offspring: keep penury afar and grant us plenty.

+Oldenberg

May he, the knowing one, distinguish wisdom and folly of mortals 1, like straight and crooked backs (of horses) 2. And for the sake of wealth and noble offspring, O god, grant us Diti and keep off Aditi 3.

+Geldner

Verstand und Unverstand der Sterblichen m├╢ge der Kundige scheiden, Recht und Unrecht der Sterblichen wie gerade und krumme R├╝cken der Rosse. Verhilf uns zu Reichtum und zu guter Nachkommenschaft, o Gott, erla├Я die Schuld, sch├╝tze die Unschuld!

+Grassmann

Verstand und Unverstand der Menschen sondre er klug wie grad’ und krumme Thieresr├╝cken; Damit o Gott uns kinderreiches Gut sei, so schenk Besitz uns, wehre ab den Mangel.

+Elizarenkova

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬThe unveiled sages abiding in the dwellings of man have glorified the sage (Agni); therefore, lord of sacrifice, you may proceed with swift-moving feet to behold the admirable and marvellous deities.тАЭ

+Jamison Brereton

The poet [=Agni] have the undeceivable poets instructed, fixing him down fast in the houses of ─Аyu.
From there, Agni, you should look with your eyes upon those who are easily seen and upon the unerring ones (who go) along the ways of the stranger.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

I take paс╕Нbh├нс╕е in this vs. as belonging to a root noun p├б┼Ы-, meaning тАШwith the eyesтАЩ, flg. Oldenberg (SBE [1897]) and Schindler (Wurzelnomen, 31). (However, Oldenberg silently retracted this view in his short piece on paс╕Нbh├нс╕е some ten years later [ZDMG 63 (1909): 300-302 [=KlsSch 316-18].) As Schindler points out, other hapaxes occur in etymological figures like our paс╕Нbh├нс╕е pa┼Ыyeс╕е. All other exx. of paс╕Нbh├нс╕е belong to p├бd- тАШfootтАЩ, including the one two vss. later (IV.2.14). Although such close proximity of identical forms might appear to weigh against assigning them to two different stems, esp. since one of the stems would be a hapax, their contexts seem designed to disambiguate: vs. 12 contains the etym. fig., while 14 juxtaposes the word with another body part frequently paired with it: paс╕Нbh├нr h├бstebhiс╕е тАЬwith feet (and) hands.тАЭ

+Griffith

This Sage the Sages, ne’er deceived, commanded, setting him down in dwellings of the living.
Hence mayst thou, friendly God, with rapid footsteps behold the Gods, wonderful, fair to look on.

+Oldenberg

The undeceived sages instructed the sage (Agni), setting him down in the dwellings of ├Вyu 1. Hence mayst thou behold, O Agni, with thy eyes 2 these beings visible and secret (that move) on the Arya’s ways 3.

+Geldner

Die untr├╝glichen Seher haben den Seher unterwiesen, als sie ihn in die Wohnung des Ayu verpflanzten. Von da aus m├╢gest du, Agni, an den F├╝├Яen diese sichtbaren Absichten und an dem Eifer des hohen Herrn seine Absichten ersehen.

+Grassmann

Den Seher wiesen an die treuen Seher, ihn niedersetzend in des Menschen H├дuser; Von dort beschaust mit Blicken Agni stets du, die sichtbar sind und unsichtbar, du holder.

тАЬTherefore, Agni, when we labour for you with hands and feet, and all our members, the pious performers of rites, (the Aс╣Еgirasas), exercise their arms in the work (of attrition), as wheelwrights fabricate a car.тАЭ

+Jamison Brereton

Then while we [=sacrificing priests] have acted, with feet, with hands, with bodies, in serving you, Agni,
like those making a chariot with the work of (our/their) two arms, those of good insight [=poets] have held fast to the truth, panting over it.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

The vs. modulates from the 1st pl. of the subordinate clause in the first hemistich (y├бd vay├бm тАж cakс╣Ыm─Б╠Б) to the 3rd pl. of the main clause of d (yemuс╕е sudhy├ас╕е) via the simile in c (r├бthaс╣Г n├б kr├бntaс╕е). The simile could belong either to the subord. cl. or the main cl. and is grammatically and semantically appropriate to either the 1st or the 3rd ps. subject of either.

On с╣Ыt├бm ─Б┼Ыuс╣г─Бn─Б╠Бс╕е see comm. ad IV.1.13.

+Griffith

Now all that we, thy faithful servants, Agni, have done with feet, with hands, and with our bodies,
The wise, with toil, the holy rite have guided, as those who frame a car with manual cunning.

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬMay we seven priests first in order engender from the material drawn the worshippers of the creator (Agni); may we Aс╣Еgirasas be the sons of heaven, and, radiant, divide the wealth-continuing mountain.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

May we, Aс╣Еgirasas, be the sons of heaven: divasputr─Б aс╣Еgiraso bhavena, or, may we, the sons of heaven be Aс╣Еgirasas; or, bh┼лtimantaс╕е, possessed of superior power. The Aс╣Еgirasas are the sons of A-ditya, aс╣Еgiras─Бm ─Бdityaputratvam ─Бmn─Бgyate; the text is: tasya yad retaс╕е prathamam udadipyata tad asau ─Бdityo abhavat, ityupakramya ye aс╣Еg─Бr─Б asanste aс╣Еgiraso abhavan, that which was his seed was first manifested as ─Аditya, thence, in succession, those which were the cinders became the Aс╣Еgirasas; wealth-containing mountain: ─Бdrim rujema dhaninam, may allude to the rock in which the cows were hidden; or, adri may be rendered cloud (megha), by the disruption of which rain is made to fall

+Jamison Brereton

Then as the seven inspired poets might we be born from mother Dawn, as the foremost ritual adepts for men.
Might we become sons of heaven, Aс╣Еgirases. Might we break the rock that holds the prize, as we blaze.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

For the third time in this hymn a p─Бda-final acc. pl. might more comfortably be interpreted as a gen. pl. – here nс╣Ы╠Д╠Бn. In the cases of m├бrt─Бn in 3d and 11b we saw that the acc. pl. reading was easily possible and an abbreviated (or re-formed) gen. pl.

interpr. was unnecessary. Here an acc. pl. interpr. seems more difficult, though perhaps not impossible. If it is a gen. pl. the tr. would be тАЬas the foremost ritual adepts of/among men,тАЭ and most interpr. implicitly or explicitly accept this analysis.

(See also disc. in AiG III.119 and Oldenberg, ZDMG 55: 285-89 [=KlSch 744-78], though Oldenberg in the Noten favors a nominative pl. analysis, also by preference ZDMG 55: 287 [=KlSch 746].) Certainly nс╣Ы╠Б╠Дn appears to be more multivalent in the RV than other acc. pl., and, though reluctant, I cannot rule out a gen. pl. However, I think it is possible that nс╣Ы╠Б╠Дn is a rough acc. of goal (тАЬborn to menтАЭ) or respect (тАЬritual adepts with respect to menтАЭ).

Interestingly, here тАЬweтАЭ aspire to a complete set of parents: Mother Dawn, Father Heaven. Generally in the RV a single parent will do in any particular rhetorical situation.

+Griffith

May we, seven sages first in rank, engender, from Dawn the Mother, men to be ordainers.
May we, Angirases, be sons of Heaven, and, radiant, burst the wealth-containing mountain.

+Oldenberg

And may we be born from the Dawn, the mother, as the seven priests 1, as the first worshippers among men 2. May we be the Aс╣Еgiras, the sons of Heaven. May we flaming break the rock which contains the prize of the contest 3.

Und wir m├╢chten als die sieben S├дnger von der Mutter Usas geboren werden als die ersten Meister unter den M├дnnern. Wir m├╢chten des Himmels S├╢hne, die Angiras┬┤ werden und inbr├╝nstig den Fels mit dem Schatz erbrechen.

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬThus, Agni, our excellent and ancient forefathers, celebrators of holy sacrifice, proceeded to (the region of) pure light, and, reciting prayers and dispersing gloom, they made manifest the purple (kine).тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Yajus. 19.69; proceeded to the region of pure light: ┼Ыucid ayan d─лdhitim d─лptam sth─Бnam tejas c─Бgacchan: ravi-maс╣Зс╕Нalam, the orb of the sun; the last phrases: may we, dividing the rays of the sun and piercing the earth (with sacrificial posts), also proceed by the path of the gods; or to heaven;

Apavran = ap─Бvс╣Ыс╣Зumaс╕е, with the sense of the potential

+Jamison Brereton

Then like our further forefathers of old, panting over the truth, o Agni, those reciting solemn speech (now) will come to the blazing (udder of sacrifice [=Vala]), to visionary power. Splitting (heaven and) earth, they (will) unclose the ruddy (cows [=dawns]).

+Jamison Brereton Notes

On с╣Ыt├бm ─Б┼Ыuс╣г─Бn─Б╠Бс╕е see comm. ad IV.1.13.

This vs. has double temporal reference, to the Aс╣Еgirases of long ago using sacred speech to split the Vala cave and release the cows and to the current priests, who imitate the speech of the Aс╣Еgirases in order to release the dawns from darkness.

The failure to realize the double reference to both the opening of Vala and the beginning of the current dawn sacrifice has caused interpretational difficulties. To begin with, ┼Ы├║ci in c has been puzzled over. Oldenberg (SBE) attempted to make it a fem. adj. modifying d─л╠Бdhitim, but in the Noten opts rather for an adverbial neut.

Most other tr. interpr. it as an abstract тАШKlarheitтАЩ vel sim. (Geldner, Renou, Scarlatta [530], sim.

Schmidt [Bс╣Ыhaspati und Indra 43-44]), while Witzel Got┼Н take it as the modifier of с╣Ыt├бm in the preceding p─Бda. I do not know of other exx. of ┼Ы├║ci- in abstract value; I interpr. it rather in conjunction with the phrase ┼Ы├║cy ┼л╠Бdhaс╕е тАж g├бv─Бm тАЬthe gleaming/blazing udder of cowsтАЭ in the preceding hymn (IV.1.19). As noted in the comm. there, I take this as a ref. to the Vala cave. But this тАЬblazing (udder)тАЭ can also refer to the current sacrifice, with the newly kindled fire at its focus. The priests approach this with their sacred speech to set the ritual in motion and achieve d─л╠Бdhitim тАШvisionary powerтАЩ.

I think p─Бda c is appropriate for both the ancient Aс╣Еgirases and the presentday ritualists, and so I would modify the published translation somewhat. The verb ayan is a subjunctive to the root present of тИЪi and therefore primarily applicable to the ritualists and the actions they will now perform. But I also think that itтАЩs possible to interpr. it as a backformed injunctive to the same root present. Since augmented imperfects to stems beginning with a vowel always have lengthened augment (here, well-attested 3rd pl. ─Бyan тАШthey wentтАЩ), it would be possible to form an injunctive by тАЬsubtractingтАЭ the augment a-, producing ayan, rather than the more proper yan (found only in III.4.5). By such an interpr. the Aс╣Еgirases could also be subjects of the verb: they came (inj.) to the gleaming/blazingVala cave (represented by ┼Ы├║ci), and the priests will come (subj.) to the gleaming/blazing place of sacrifice.

The Pp. reads kс╣г─Б╠Бm─Б in d as kс╣г─Б╠Бma, and most interpr. (save for Witzel Got┼Н) follow the Pp. and take this form as a singular, tr. тАЬsplitting the earthтАЭ – as a reference only to the Vala myth (even though it is not the earth that gets split in that myth). But I think we should take the Saс╣Гhit─Б form seriously, as the elliptical dual it appears to be, extracted from the dual dvandva dy─Б╠Бv─Б-kс╣г─Б╠Бm─Б. The phrase тАЬsplitting (heaven and) earthтАЭ would refer to the visual experience of dawn, when the appearance of the dawn light at the horizon seems to split sky from earth, allowing the light to flood in through the resulting slit.

+Griffith

As in the days of old our ancient Fathers, speeding the work of holy worship, Agni,
Sought pure light and devotion, singing praises; they cleft the ground and made red Dawns apparent.

+Oldenberg

And as our first, ancient fathers, O Agni, were aspiring after Rita 1тАФthey attained to pure devotion 2, chanting their litanies. Cleaving the earth they disclosed the red (cows).

+Geldner

Und wie unsere fernsten Ahnen, die sich vor alters f├╝r das Rechte ereiferten, o Agni, so m├╢gen jetzt die in Liedern Redenden zur Klarheit, zur Erkenntnis kommen. Den Boden spaltend sollen sie die r├╢tlichen Usas aufdecken.

+Grassmann

Als unsre V├дter, sie die fr├╝hern, alten, anfachten einst das heil’ge Feur, o Agni, Da gingen strahlend zum Gebet die S├дnger, den Boden spaltend fanden sie die K├╝he.

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬPerformers of good works, brilliant and devout, the praises of the gods have freed their birth from impurity, as (a smith heats) bronze; exciting Agni, elevating Indra, and wandering about (in search), they have gone to the vast (hidden) herd of cattle.тАЭ

+Jamison Brereton

Those of good work and good light, seeking the gods, smelting the races of the gods like metal,
they went blazing, strengthening Agni and Indra, besieging the cattle pen.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

And yet again we have a form that would be best interpr. as a genitive pl., but formally is not – dev─Б╠Бor dev─Б╠Бс╕е [so Pp.] in dev─Б╠Бj├бnim─Б (cf. dev─Б╠Бn─Бm тАж j├бnima [or j├бnim─Б] in the next vs., 18b). It would be possible to interpr. dev─Б╠Бс╕е as nominative subj. in the simile (тАЬas the gods do metalтАЭ); on the other hand, reading dev─Б╠Б, some have taken it as a neut. pl. adj. with j├бnim─Б. Here, however, I think a gen. pl. interpr.

is the correct one, but the poet is playing a little trick: the sequence n├б dev─Б╠Бis to be flipped to *dev─Б╠Бna ├а dev─Б╠Бn─Б(с╣Г). The occurrence of the expected phrase in the next vs. would be an example of immediate poetic repair (see my 2003 тАЬPoetic ‘Repair’ in the Rig VedaтАЭ).

The standard tr. take ┼Ыuc├бntaс╕е as transitive, with agn├нm as obj., but as most comment, verb forms to this root are otherwise intransitive; see esp. identical ┼Ыuc├бntaс╕е in nearby 15d. It seems better to interpr. agn├нm as the obj. of vavс╣Ыdh├бntaс╕е along with ├нndram; there is no obstacle to such an interpr. On the secondary present stem seen in the participle vavс╣Ыdh├бnt- here, cf. K├╝mmel (471).

+Griffith

Gods, doing holy acts, devout, resplendent, smelting like ore their human generations.
Enkindling Agni and exalting Indra, they came encompassing the stall of cattle.

+Oldenberg

The pious men, well performing the acts (of worship), resplendent, melting 1 the generations of the gods 2 like ore 3, kindling Agni, strengthening Indra, went along 4, besieging the stall of cows.

+Geldner

Die Guteswirkenden, Erleuchteten, Gottergebenen sind gekommen. Ihn anfachend, schwei├Яend wie Erz, wie die G├╢tter, die die Menschengeschlechter zusammenschwei├Яten, das Feuer entflammend, den Indra st├дrkend, indem sie die Rinderh├╢hle belagern.

+Grassmann

Die lichten G├╢tter, kunstreich, G├╢tter liebend, durch Blasen zeugend ihn, sowie das Eisen, Entz├╝ndend Agni und den Indra st├дrkend, umlagernd drangen sie zum Stall der K├╝he. 18. Wie fette Heerden Viehes sah der starke nah vor sich stehn die g├╢ttlichen Geschlechter; Es flehten da der Menschen heisse W├╝nsche, zu segnen auch die k├╝nft’gen, treuen M├дnner.

+Elizarenkova

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬFierce (Agni), when (Indra) proclaimed the near presence of the herd of the kine of the divine (Aс╣Еgirasas) as a herd of cattle in a well-stored stall, the progeny of mortals were thereby enabled (to perform pious acts), and the master of the family rendered competent to (provide for) the increase of posterity and (the support of) dependants.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Herd of cattle: ─Бy┼лtheva kс╣гumati pa┼Ыvoс╕е akhyat dev─Бn─Бm yaj janim─Бni = liс╣н, like a herd in food-possessing animals, he has said to the gods that which birth is nigh;

Jan─Бm─Б = go saс╣Еgham; mart─Бn─Бm cid urva┼Ы─лrakс╣Ыpranvс╣Ыdhe cid arya uprasya ayoс╕е: urva┼Ыiс╕е = praj─Б,progeny;

Akс╣Ыpran = were made able (cf. Nirukta 5.13: urva┼Ыiс╕е = apsaras, i.e. urvabhya a┼Ыnuta;or, urubhy─Бm a┼Ыnuta, who pervades or proceeds from the thigh. The legend is that Urva┼Ыi was born from the thigh of N─Бr─Бyaс╣Зa

+Jamison Brereton

He [=Agni?] watched over them like (a herdsman) the herds of livestock in a cattle-rich (pasture)тАФwatched over the race of gods that was nearby, o strong one.
The Urva┼Ы─лs yearned also for (the race of) men, also for the increase of the stranger, of ─Аyu to come.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

This vs. closes the mythological section of the hymn and is so positioned to seem as if it ought to be the denouement of the Vala myth. But it seems, at least to me, to have no connection with that myth or, indeed, with anything else in this hymn.

I remain baffled by it, and my comments here will be only on matters of detail.

Geldner (/Witzel Got┼Н) take the subj. of ab to be the leader of the Aс╣Еgirases, possibly Bс╣Ыhaspati. I follow Oldenberg (Noten) and Renou in taking Agni as 3rd ps. subj., though he is also addressed with the voc. ugra. In this vs. the discrepancy in person is the least of our problems. My rather weak reason for preferring Agni as subj. is the fact that the hymn, dedicated to Agni, is drawing to a close, and the final two vss. (19-20) are explicitly Agni vss. I see nothing in the vs. to suggest that any Aс╣Еgiras is involved, save for the herds of livestock that remind us of the Vala myth – but they are in a simile.

Geldner takes ─Б╠БтИЪkhy─Б as meaning тАШcountтАЩ, but as Renou points out, this sense is not found earlier than the ┼ЪB. A parallel passage shows a clear word for тАШwatch over, look atтАЩ: VII.60.3 s├бс╣Г y├│ y┼лth├йva j├бnim─Бni c├бс╣гс╣нe, which supports тАШwatch overтАЩ for the verb here. That passage also suggests that the j├бnima in b is the obj. of ─Б╠БтАж akhyat and corresponds to y┼лth─Б╠Бin the simile (similar Oldenberg, Noten). I therefore take the y├бd in b to be a neut. sg. referring to j├бnima rather than the subordinating conj. (тАШwhen, sinceтАЩ) of the standard tr. – and I also follow the Pp in taking sg. j├бnima as the underlying form in the sandhi conglomeration j├бnim─Б╠Бnti, rather than pl. j├бnim─Б as assumed by others. (The j├бnim─Б of 17b does give me pause, however.) With Oldenberg I supply тАШpastureтАЩ with kс╣гum├бti in p─Бda, rather than taking it as a personal designation (Viehbesitzer, ma├оtre du b├йtail), though not much depends on it. In my (/OldenbergтАЩs) reading, it would refer to the ritual ground. OldenbergтАЩs paraphrase of the first hemistich in the Noten is тАЬтАж dass Agni тАж vor sich die G├╢tterscharen erblickte wie Viehherden auf der Weides des Opfers.тАЭ His interpr. of the passage informed mine.

As to what the тАЬnearbyтАЭ race of gods consists of, I have no idea – perhaps the gods that come to the sacrifice. Recall that in vss. 3-4 the poet asked Agni to bring (only) a selection of gods to the sacrifice.

The second half-vs. is even more puzzling than the first, because there seems no reason to introduce Urva┼Ы─л and her retinue (pl. urva┼Ы─л╠Бс╕е) and her son ─Аyu. I supply j├бnima with m├бrt─Бn─Бm rather than construing this gen. independently as most others do; the parallelism of the passage supports this.

+Griffith

Strong One! he marked them-and the Gods before them-like herds of cattle in a foodful pasture.
There they moaned forth their strong desire for mortals, to aid the True, the nearest One, the Living.

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬWe have worshipped you (Agni), and have thereby become the performers of a good work, adoring the full and variously delighting Agni, the beautiful lustre of the radiant divinity, when the brilliant dawns have arrayed (themselves) in light.тАЭ

+Jamison Brereton

We have acted for you; we have been good workersтАФ(as) the radiant dawns have clothed themselves in truthтАФ
we always grooming in many ways unfailing Agni, beautifully gleaming, the dear eye of the god.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

The augmented 3rd pl. avasran is listed as an aor. to тИЪvas тАШshineтАЩ by Whitney (Rts) and Grassmann and so tr. by Oldenberg (SBE), Renou, and (somewhat attenuated) Geldner I take it rather as an impf. to the root pres. of тИЪvas тАШwearтАЩ (so listed by Lubotsky, so interpr., more or less, by K├╝mmel, Stativ, 97-98); Witzel Got┼Н take it also to тАШwearтАЩ, but as an ingressive aorist. Since the root already has a root present and there are no other forms to a root aorist, this seems to multiply entities unnecessarily. What does it mean for the dawns to wear/clothe themselves in truth? Perhaps either that they are greeted by a (truly formulated) hymn that serves as their garment or that by dawning they display the truth of the orderly functioning cosmos as their clothing. Although I think that avasran belongs properly to тИЪvas тАШwearтАЩ, this of course does not mean that there is not a pun on тИЪvas тАШdawn, shineтАЩ.

+Griffith

We have worked for thee, we have laboured nobly-bright Dawns have shed their light upon our worship-
Adding a beauty to the perfect Agni, and the God’s beauteous eye that shines for ever.

+Oldenberg

We have done our work for thee; we have been good workersтАФthe brilliant dawns have shone out Rita 1,тАФbrightening 2 the perfect Agni who manifoldly shines with fine splendour, (brightening) the god’s beautiful eye.

+Geldner

Wir haben f├╝r dich geschafft, wir sind gute Arbeiter gewesen - rechtzeitig sind die strahlenden Morgenr├╢ten aufgegangen - den vollkommenen Agni, den vielfach schimmernden, das sch├╢ne Auge des Gottes herausputzend.

+Grassmann

Wir dienten dir und waren eifrig th├дtig, rechtzeitig strahlten hell die Morgenr├╢then, Den Agni schm├╝ckend, den vollkommnen, pr├дcht’gen, des Gottes Auge, welches weithin leuchtet.

+Elizarenkova

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬCreator, Agni, we have repeated these your praises to you who are all-wise; do you accept them;blaze aloft; make us opulent; do you who are worshipped by many bestow upon us ample wealth.тАЭ

+Jamison Brereton

These solemn speeches have we spoken to you the poet, o Agni, you ritual adept: enjoy them.
Blaze up; make us better off. Extend to us great riches, o you of many favors.

+Griffith

Agni, Disposer, we have sung these praises to thee the Wise: do thou accept them gladly.
Blaze up on high and ever make us richer. Give us great wealth, O thou whose boons are many.

+Oldenberg

We have recited these hymns for thee, the sage, O Agni, worshipper (of the gods) 1; accept them! Blaze up; make us wealthier. Bestow great wealth on us, O bountiful one!

+Geldner
